construction workers that are provided by the Contractor at the site, and the costs of transportation, installation, 
dismantling, minor repairs, and removal of such temporary facilities, machinery, equipment, and hand tools. Rates 
and quantities of equipment owned by the Contractor, or a related party as defined in Section 7.8, shall be subject to 
the Agent’s prior approval and current comparable quotes for like items shall be provided to Agent upon request. The 
total rental cost of any such equipment may not exceed the rental rate for a like item from a national rental retailer in 
the Project’s locale, but in no event shall the total of such rental charges exceed the fair market value of the equipment 
when first utilized on the Project.  Contractor shall secure a competitive and reasonable rental rate available for the 
rented facilities, machines and equipment and shall only rent such facilities upon need.  When rented facilities, 
machines and equipment are no longer needed to perform the Work, Contractor shall return such items back to the 
vendor. Contractor shall not be reimbursed for any costs for rented facilities, machines and equipment where the rented 
facilities, machines and equipment is no longer needed to perform the Work.. 
 
§ 7.5.3 Costs of removal of debris from the site of the Work and its proper and legal disposal.

§ 7.8 Related Party Transactions 
§ 7.8.1 For purposes of this Section 7.8, the term “related party” shall mean (1) a parent, subsidiary, affiliate, or other 
entity having common ownership of, or sharing common management with, the Contractor; (2) any entity in which 
any stockholder in, or management employee of, the Contractor holds an equity interest in excess of ten percent in the 
aggregate; (3) any entity which has the right to control the business or affairs of the Contractor; or (4) any person, or 
any member of the immediate family of any person, who has the right to control the business or affairs of the 
Contractor. 
 
§ 7.8.2 If any of the costs to be reimbursed arise from a transaction between the Contractor and a related party, the 
Contractor shall notify the Agent of the specific nature of the contemplated transaction, including the identity of the 
related party and the anticipated cost to be incurred, before any such transaction is consummated or cost incurred. If 
the Agent, after such notification, authorizes the proposed transaction in writing, then the cost incurred shall be 
included as a cost to be reimbursed, and the Contractor shall procure the Work, equipment, goods, or service, from 
the related party, as a Subcontractor, according to the terms of Article 10. If the Agent fails to authorize the transaction 
in writing, the Contractor shall procure the Work, equipment, goods, or service from some person or entity other than 
a related party according to the terms of Article 10. In no event shall the charges of a “related party” be in excess of 
those from a comparable unrelated entity. 
 
ARTICLE 8   COSTS NOT TO BE REIMBURSED 
§ 8.1 The Cost of the Work shall not include the items listed below: 
.1      Salaries and other compensation of the Contractor’s personnel stationed at the Contractor’s principal 
office or offices other than the site office, except as specifically provided in Section 7.2, or as may be 
provided in Article 15; 
.2       Bonuses, profit sharing, incentive compensation, and any other discretionary payments, paid to anyone 
hired by the Contractor or paid to any Subcontractor or vendor, unless the Agent has provided prior 
approval; 
.3      Expenses of the Contractor’s principal office and offices other than the site office; 
.4      Overhead and general expenses, except as may be expressly included in Article 7; 
.5      The Contractor’s capital expenses, including interest on the Contractor’s capital employed for the Work; 
.6        Except as provided in Section 7.7.3 of this Agreement, costs due to the negligence of, or failure to 
fulfill a specific responsibility of the Contract by, the Contractor, Subcontractors, and suppliers, or 
anyone directly or indirectly employed by any of them or for whose acts any of them may be liable, 
including but not limited to the correction of defective Work and the disposal of materials or equipment 
improperly supplied; 
.7      Any cost not specifically and expressly described in Article 7;  
.8       Costs, other than costs included in Change Orders approved by the Agent, that would cause the 
Guaranteed Maximum Price to be exceeded; 
.9       Costs and expenses arising from Contractor’s indemnity obligations under the Contract Documents;  
.10     Penalties and/or fines assessed against Contractor for failure to comply with laws, statutes,  
          regulations, rules, codes, and/or ordinances;  
.11     Losses associated with damaged, lost or stolen tools and equipment unless caused by the Owner,  
          Architect, their agents or employees, the Owner's separate contractors or anyone for whose acts the  
          Owner may be liable;  
.12     Deductibles and co-payments on insurance policies except as stated otherwise in the Contract  
          Documents;  
.13     Costs associated with the replacement of lost or damaged property not covered under Builder’s Risk  
          Insurance to the extent caused by the Contractor, its subcontractors or anyone whose acts they  
          may be liable;  
.14     Costs for satisfying or discharging any lien claim relating to work paid for by Owner  
.15     Costs associated with remedying, remediating and/or correcting any condition caused by the  
          negligence of Contractor, its subcontractors or anyone whose acts they may be liable; and  
.16     Costs incurred by Contractor for items that Contractor is obligated to perform at its own expense or  
          cost pursuant to the Contract Documents or where the Contract Documents expressly state that  
          Contractor is to bear the costs or expense thereof.

ARTICLE 9   DISCOUNTS, REBATES AND REFUNDS 
§ 9.1 Cash discounts obtained on payments made by the Contractor shall accrue to the Owner. Trade discounts, rebates, 
refunds, and amounts received from sales of surplus materials and equipment shall accrue to the Owner, and the 
Contractor shall make provisions so that they can be obtained. 
 
§ 9.2 Amounts that accrue to the Owner in accordance with the provisions of Section 9.1 shall be credited to the Owner 
as a deduction from the Cost of the Work. 
 
ARTICLE 10   SUBCONTRACTS AND OTHER AGREEMENTS 
§ 10.1 Those portions of the Work that the Contractor does not customarily perform with the Contractor’s own 
personnel shall be performed under subcontracts or other appropriate agreements with the Contractor. The Agent may 
designate specific persons from whom, or entities from which, the Contractor shall obtain bids. The Contractor shall 
obtain bids from Subcontractors, and from suppliers of materials or equipment fabricated especially for the Work, 
who are qualified to perform that portion of the Work in accordance with the requirements of the Contract Documents. 
The Contractor shall deliver such bids, along with a copy of the scope sheets for each bid, if requested, to the Agent 
with an indication as to which bids the Contractor intends to accept. Where possible, the Contractor shall obtain, at a 
minimum, three (3) competitive bids from major  (Subcontracts in excess of $150,000) Subcontractors and major 
suppliers and provide Owner with same together with a deliverable showing the bid tabs for all 
divisions/subcontractors for review.  The Owner and Agent then have the rights to review the Contractor’s list of 
proposed subcontractors and suppliers and, subject to Section 10.1.1, to object to any subcontractor or supplier. Any 
approval or objection by the Owner or Agent shall not relieve the Contractor of its responsibility to perform the Work 
in accordance with the Contract Documents. The Contractor shall not be required to contract with anyone to whom 
the Contractor has reasonable objection. 
 
§ 10.1.1 When a specific subcontractor or supplier (1) is recommended to the Agent by the Contractor; (2) is qualified 
to perform that portion of the Work; and (3) has submitted a bid that conforms to the requirements of the Contract 
Documents without reservations or exceptions, but the Owner or Agent requires that another bid be accepted, then the 
Contractor may require that a Change Order be issued to adjust the Guaranteed Maximum Price by the difference 
between the bid of the person or entity recommended to the Agent by the Contractor and the amount of the subcontract 
or other agreement actually signed with the person or entity designated by the Owner or Agent.  If the Contractor 
recommends an award of a contract to a Subcontractor or supplier that is not the lowest bidder for an item of the Work, 
the Contractor shall provide Owner with written justification for such recommendation. 
 
§ 10.2 Subcontracts or other agreements shall conform to the applicable payment provisions of this Agreement, and 
shall be subject to the approval of Agent, which shall not be unreasonably withheld. Subcontracts shall not be awarded 
on the basis of cost plus a fee without the Agent’s prior written approval. If a subcontract is awarded on the basis of 
cost plus a fee, the Contractor shall provide in the subcontract for the Agent to receive the same audit rights with 
regard to the Subcontractor as the Agent receives with regard to the Contractor in Article 11. 
 
ARTICLE 11   ACCOUNTING RECORDS 
The Contractor shall keep full and detailed records and accounts related to the Cost of the Work, and exercise such 
controls, as may be necessary for proper financial management under this Contract and to substantiate all costs 
incurred. The accounting and control systems shall be satisfactory to the Agent. The Agent, Owner and the Owner’s 
auditors shall, during regular business hours and upon reasonable notice, be afforded access to, and shall be permitted 
to audit and copy, the Contractor’s records and accounts, including complete documentation supporting accounting 
entries, books, job cost reports, correspondence, instructions, drawings, receipts, subcontracts, Subcontractor’s 
proposals, Subcontractor’s invoices, purchase orders, vouchers, memoranda, and other data relating to this Contract. 
The Contractor shall preserve these records for a period of three years after final payment, or for such longer period 
as may be required by law.

§ 12.1.1 Based upon Applications for Payment submitted to the Agent and Architect by the Contractor, and Certificates

of the Contract Sum, to the Contractor, as provided below and elsewhere in the Contract Documents.  Contractor has 
provided Owner instructions and all necessary forms required by Owner to effectuate payment to Contractor by wire 
transfer or check. If Owner receives a request to change such payment information, Owner agrees that it will not

§ 12.1.2 The period covered by each Application for Payment shall be one calendar month ending on the last day of 
the month. 
 
§ 12.1.3 Provided that a true and accurate Application for Payment with supporting detail is received by the Agent not 
later than the 25th day of a calendar month, the Owner shall make payment of the amount certified to the Contractor 
not later than 30 days after the first day of the following calendar month. If an Application for Payment is received by 
the Agent after the application date fixed above  payment of the amount certified shall be made by the Owner not later 
than thirty (30) days after the first day of the following calendar month after Agent receives the true and accurate 
Application for Payment.  . Contractor is to provide a “pencil copy” of their Application for Payment no later than the 
20th day of a calendar month. 
 
§ 12.1.4 The Application for Payment shall be made in the AIA G702 and G703 format based on actual percentages 
of completion. With each Application for Payment, the Contractor shall submit payrolls, petty cash accounts, receipted 
invoices or invoices with check vouchers attached, and any other evidence required by the Agent to demonstrate that 
payments already made by the Contractor on account of the Cost of the Work equal or exceed progress payments 
already received by the Contractor plus payrolls for the period covered by the present Application for Payment, less 
that portion of the progress payments attributable to the Contractor’s Fee. 
 
§ 12.1.5 Each Application for Payment shall be based on the most recent schedule of values submitted by the Contractor 
in accordance with the Contract Documents. The schedule of values shall allocate the entire Guaranteed Maximum 
Price among: (1) the various portions of the Work; (2) any contingency for costs that are included in the Guaranteed 
Maximum Price but not otherwise allocated to another line item or included in a Change Order; and (3) the 
Contractor’s Fee. 
 
§ 12.1.5.1 The schedule of values shall be prepared in such form and supported by such data to substantiate its accuracy 
as the Agent may require. The schedule of values shall be used as a basis for reviewing the Contractor’s Applications 
for Payment.  Notwithstanding the above, the Owner acknowledges that the Project is not a line item GMP and that 
during the subcontractor buyout process the Contractor shall be able to reallocate the schedule of values.  
 
§ 12.1.5.2 The allocation of the Guaranteed Maximum Price under this Section 12.1.5 shall not constitute a separate 
guaranteed maximum price for the Cost of the Work of each individual line item in the schedule of values. 
 
§ 12.1.5.3 Should there be savings from any particular line item once that line item buyout is complete, the Contractor 
shall reallocate the savings into a  separate line item designated as “Buyout Savings”. This “Buyout Savings” shall 
function as the aggregate repository for use in balancing line items until buyout is complete. The Buyout Savings is 
to be exhausted prior to the Contractor requesting the Agent’s approval for any reallocation of the construction 
contingency.  
The Contractor shall submit a buyout and contingency use log with each application for payment.  
 
§ 12.1.6 Applications for Payment shall show the percentage of completion of each portion of the Work as of the end 
of the period covered by the Application for Payment. The percentage of completion shall be the lesser of (1) the 
percentage of that portion of the Work which has actually been completed; or (2) the percentage obtained by dividing 
(a) the expense that has actually been incurred by the Contractor on account of that portion of the Work and for which 
the Contractor has made payment or intends to make payment prior to the next Application for Payment, by (b) the 
share of the Guaranteed Maximum Price allocated to that portion of the Work in the schedule of values. 
 
§ 12.1.7 In accordance with AIA Document A201–2017 and subject to other provisions of the Contract Documents, 
the amount of each progress payment shall be computed as follows: 
 
§ 12.1.7.1 The amount of each progress payment shall first include:

§ 12.1.8 Retainage 
§ 12.1.8.1 For each progress payment made prior to Substantial Completion of the Work, the Owner may withhold the 
following amount, as retainage, from the payment otherwise due: 
 
Ten (10%) percent.  Retainage shall not be held on Fee, General Conditions and Insurance.   
 
§ 12.1.8.1.1 Reserved. 
 
§ 12.1.8.2 Subject to Agent’s approval, reduction or limitation of retainage, if any, shall be as follows: 
 
Upon fifty (50%) percent of Substantial Completion of the Work, Contractor may submit for a reduction of the 
retainage, so that the remaining retainage shall not be less than 5% of the Contract Sum.  The retained amount shall 
be reduced to five (5%) percent on all future applications for payment. At the Owner’s reasonable discretion, , 
retainage may not be released for line items where the Owner reasonably believes it is necessary to protect its 
interests and ensure any incomplete Work is properly completed.  
 
 
§ 12.1.8.3 Upon achieving Substantial Completion of the entire Work, the Owner shall continue to hold until final 
completion of the entire Work (including but not limited to punchlist Work) TWO HUNDRED PERCENT (200%) of 
the Owner’s reasonable estimate of the value of the punchlist Work, any Claims the Owner may have, and all other 
amounts that the Owner is entitled to withhold. Retainage with respect to punchlist Work shall be paid upon 
completion of all such punchlist items to the reasonable satisfaction of the Owner. In no event shall the Owner be 
required to disburse any funds on account of retainage prior to the time such sums are payable pursuant to the 
applicable subcontract unless the delay in completion is due to the acts or omissions of the Owner or others over whom 
the Contractor has no control.  In such a case, the Contractor may invoice for the punchlist work on a monthly basis. 
 
§ 12.1.9 If final completion of the Work is materially delayed through no fault of the Contractor, the Owner shall pay 
the Contractor any additional amounts in accordance with Article 9 of AIA Document A201–2017.

§ 12.2 Final Payment 
§ 12.2.1 Final payment, constituting the entire unpaid balance of the Contract Sum, shall be made by the Owner to the 
Contractor when 
.1    the Contractor has fully performed the Contract, except for the Contractor’s responsibility to correct 
Work as provided in Article 12 of AIA Document A201–2017, and to satisfy other requirements, if any, 
which extend beyond final payment; 
.2    the Contractor has submitted a final accounting for the Cost of the Work and a final Application for 
Payment;  
.3    a final Certificate for Payment has been issued by the Architect in accordance with Section 12.2.2;  
.4    the Contractor has provided to Agent a complete set of required close-out documents, including all 
warranties, as-built drawings, manuals and, in person systems training (including training video 
recordings) for the operation and maintenance of all equipment, certificates of occupancy, permits, keys, 
attic stock and any other documentation necessary for the occupancy, operation, and maintenance of the 
Work and Project; 
.5 there is a fully executed AIA Document G706 entitled “Contractor’s Affidavit of Payment of Debts and 
Claims”; and 
.6 the Contractor submits to Owner lien waivers (in the form required by the state where the Project is 
located) executed by Contractor and its Subcontractors in a form satisfactory to Owner and Owner’s 
lender. 
 
§ 12.2.2 Within 30 days of the Agent’s receipt of the Contractor’s final accounting for the Cost of the Work, the Owner 
or Agent shall conduct an audit of the Cost of the Work or notify the Contractor that it will not conduct an audit. 
 
§ 12.2.2.1 If the Owner or Agent conducts an audit of the Cost of the Work, the Owner or Agent shall, within 10 days 
after completion of the audit, submit a written report based upon the auditors’ findings to the Contractor. 
 
§ 12.2.2.2 Within seven days after receipt of the written report described in Section 12.2.2.1, or receipt of notice that 
the Owner or Agent will not conduct an audit, and provided that the other conditions of Section 12.2.1 have been met, 
the Agent will either issue to the Owner a final Certificate for Payment with a copy to the Contractor, or notify the 
Contractor and Owner in writing of the Agent’s reasons for withholding a certificate as provided in Article 9 of AIA

writing to a binding dispute resolution method other than litigation, Claims will be resolved by litigation in a court of 
competent jurisdiction.

DOCUMENTS, OR ANY PROCEEDING IN ANY WAY ARISING OUT OF OR RELATED TO ANY OF THE

TRIED BEFORE A COURT AND NOT BEFORE A JURY.

Scope of Work  
Division 2 - Demolition 
Demolition of the existing entry vestibule, exterior brick walls and coping, DFH, glazing, and 
metal paneling based on new exterior finishes. Assumes existing brick lintel to support brick 
above any window to be removed. Includes demolition of exterior metal stair, catwalk, and roof 
ladders. Includes demolition of 3rd  story “pop up” structure and 2 nd  floor electrical room. 
Includes demolition of dunnage posts. Includes removal of existing metal deck as indicated to be 
replaced. Includes removal of exterior basement stair hand and guard rails. Includes removal of 
two exterior pads to be replaced at entries. Includes demolition of six interior stairs. Includes 
demolition of glazing with existing elevator shaft. Includes grinding of assumed 50% of concrete 
slabs to remove adhesive for future floor finishes. Includes removal of Building #714 interior 
finishes and removal of existing door and windows to be replaced. Includes debris removal, 
dumpsters, and hauling. Excludes salvage of existing materials for reuse. Excludes demolition of 
items not specifically identified on plans.  
Division 3 - Concrete 
Furnish and install new footings, column piers, and slab on grade for architectural column build 
outs at main entry and new entry vestibule. Includes a $10,000 allowance for miscellaneous slab 
on grade infills after completion of interior demolition by others. Includes stone and slab on 
grade infills. Includes slab on metal deck infills at one stair removal location. Includes slab on 
metal deck infills around Stair #2 at demolished metal plate flooring as well as the high bay area 
south of Stair #2, 2nd  floor electrical room openings, and demolished raised projector room floor. 
Includes metal pan stair infills at four locations. Includes concrete encasement of vertical duct 
bank riser. Includes two exterior concrete pads and stairs at side entrances. Includes two 
interior stairs at second floor warehouse area. Excludes any repair to loading dock.  
Division 3 – Cementitious Decks and Underlayment Allowance 
Includes $300,000 allowance for floor leveling.  
Division 4 - Masonry 
Furnish and install lintels, 8” CMU foundation walls at column build outs at main entry and new 
entry vestibule. Includes full height 8” CMU at two elevations as indicated. Includes 8” CMU 
stem walls along glazing elevations as indicated. Includes 8’ CMU infill at section of damaged 
exterior wall. Includes selective demo, furnishing and setting of concrete lintels, and patching of 
jambs for new openings in existing walls as indicated. Proposal assumes brick above existing 
strip windows is supported by existing structure and does not require additional support. 
Includes masonry infills at exterior doors, windows, and louvers to be demolished. Includes a 
$25,000 allowance for miscellaneous patch and repair of existing brick.  
Division 5 – Structural Steel 
Fabricate and erect new structural steel as indicated. Includes lateral bracing of new CMU walls 
at existing column locations for two new CMU elevations. Includes roof expansion and column

height in existing stairwells as well as IDF room only; work listed above will have dry vertical 
standpipes capped for connection to future T/I scope of work. A new Stortz connection and 
Knox Box is provided at the completion of the tenant scope of work. The noted scope of work 
above is not connected to any fire protection systems and shall be left inactive; the above-
mentioned scope of work is below the minimum code and will not allow occupancy. Fire 
protection piping to be carbon steel ERW sch. 10 or 40 with Victaulic valves/fittings.  
Miscellaneous: Assumes hydraulic calculations, testing/inspections and signed and sealed 
sprinkler design/shop drawings for submission to local AHJ for permits will be by the T/I scope of 
work. (1)-year warranty is included as are O&M Manuals and as-built documents for core and 
shell only.

switch over event will take place to transfer services to the new equipment; existing 
underground feeders to the existing transformer are abandoned in place. We assume utilizing 
existing conduits from building 713 to 714 for all communication/security wiring. Includes

panels assuming within 50’ of each. Includes ARC flash/breaker studies after the tenant project 
is complete. The fire alarm scope shall be a new addressable fire alarm system and annunciator 
panel, by Siemens, capable of supporting the entire building; the above-mentioned scope of 
work is below the minimum code and will not allow occupancy. All remaining code required fire 
alarm work (inclusive of testing, permitting, etc. for all AHJ requirements) is to be part of the T/I 
scope of work. Includes a new building lightning protection system installed based on concealed 
copper per UL96A/NFPA780 standards to a new building ground ring. Includes rough-ins for LL 
and ISP fiber line(s) and building exterior door security devices. A new mini-split for the LL-MDF 
room only has been included.

EXHIBIT F
Required Closeout Documentation
This section serves as a checklist to be used in compiling required project closeout documentation.  It is the
intent of this section to establish a uniform, consistent method by which all contractors shall provide
closeout documentation. This list is not represented as exhaustive; the Owner retains the right to edit this
list, including reasonable additions, through the course of the project. In the event that the required format
for closeout paperwork is unclear, then it is imperative that the contractor request clarification on what
needs to be submitted.  Final project retainage shall not be released until all required documentation is
submitted in the proper format, reviewed and approved by MRA.  Owner reserves the right to have closeout
documentation professionally prepared, if documentation is not received complete within one month of
substantial completion.  The cost of this service, if required, will be deducted from the contractor’s final
payment.
General Requirements:
 2 complete hard copies and 1 electronic file of all required project closeout documentation shall be
provided.
 All required documentation shall be provided in one complete, organized, coordinated set.
 All documentation shall be prepared in a professional manner by qualified project en gineering staff.
“As-Built” Record Drawings:
 All CAD based work shall be provided on the latest release of Autocad or compatible DXF or DWG
drawing format.
 If non-CAD based drawings are allowed, then all drawings shall be prepared by personnel who are
skilled as a draftsmen competent to prepare required drawings.  All site kept as -built markups shall be
transferred to a clean “new” set of drawings.
 Give particular attention to concealed work, which would be difficult to measure and record at a later
date.
Required Items:
X CAD based Architectural Drawings – 2 hard copies and 1 electronic file (electronic copy)
X CAD based Mechanical, Electrical, Sprinkler – 2 hard copies and 1 electronic file (electronic
copy)
X 2 Hard copies BAS Drawings with all control points, and program sequence of operations
X As-Builts not CAD based – provide 2 hard copies and one reproducible copy.
Operation and Maintenance Manuals:
 Information from all trades including the general contractor shall be compiled in one complete white 3 -
ring binder.  Binders shall be the minimum size required to hold all documentation.
 All binders shall be clearly labeled (typed) on the front cover and side spine with Title of
Manual/Binder, Owner, project name and date of substantial completion.
 A complete index / table of contents shall be provided for the manual.  The manual shall be tabbed to
correspondence to the index.   Within each tabbed section an index shall be provided, as each section
requires.
 Where originals of certain documents are provided (ie. Certificates of Occupancy) all originals shall be
included together in the same binder.
